WOW!!! This tuna steak was insanely good. I followed the recipe exactly, except I pan seared the tuna for 3 minutes on each side instead of grilling it.  I let the steaks marinade for 2 hours and then rest at room temperature for 10 minutes before cooking it. The fish came out awesome, so juicy and wonderfully tasty - I loved it (and I don't even like fish). I will make this again and again and again. Thanks Carin!

text:
Five stars, no question. Flavorful, juicy, piquant. I quartered the recipe (just cooking for me), cooked it in a skillet and just dumped the whole mix in. I had to substitute teriyaki sauce (had no soya), which may have made it lighter than the original recipe; I enjoyed it this way. I also used dried herbs, found it okay. If I could make it differently I might crust some whole garlic slices right on to the tuna steak, but this is a bit of an unnecessary flourish. If your tuna comes out "tough and chewy" you are cooking it too long. Turn the heat up way high (skillet) or get the coals really going (grill) and sear it. Unless you buy bottom-quality tuna (which you should not), it is safe to cook until the top and bottom are seared but the center is still mostly pink and relatively uncooked. The bacteria grow on the exposed parts, which is why you have to cook the heck out of any ground meat (because the exposed parts have been moved all through the meat).

text:
awesome! i followed the recipe - excpet for the following: replaced the soy sauce with Dales seasoning for meat and fish (its' soy based but as added flavor.) Also added chopped green onions (1/4 cup) and a 3/4 tsp rosemary. used fresh garlic (a must in my book!) 

i cooked the fish on a skillet. Turned the gas on high and let the pan heat up with a little bit of non-stick cooking spray on it. 

heres the best tip (got it from the man behind the fresh fish counter at Whole Foods) - turn the Tuna Steaks every 30 seconds for 3-5 minutes (depending on size of the steak)... perfectly cooked! DO NOT OVER COOK THESE. i had actually intially undercooked them (only 3 minutes). I wanted them to be cooked a little more, so i put them back in the frying pan and seared for 30 more seconds on each side.

yummy!!!!!!

text:
This was the perfect solution for the not-quite-sushi-grade tuna I allowed to sit in the fridge for 2 days. Tuna is usually dry as a bone unless served rare, but the tuna I was using was in no condition to be served rare... without this marinade, that is! I didn't give 5 stars for 2 reasons (okay, 3 reasons, the first being that I'm extremely picky!!) Reason 2: A modification that is a MUST: I dipped the fish in italian breadcrumbs prior to pan-searing in lemon olive oil- the crust was the best part. And this allowed me to serve it rare-ish still. Next reason: I thought the following point needed clarifying: this marinade has acid in it, so it "cooks" the fish ceviche-style (a good thing-- helps to eliminate some of the fishy factor.) A word of caution, though: never, ever your fish to sit in an acid-containing marinade for over 30 minutes (some say 20!) Doing so will "overcook" it (the acid, doing the ceviche thing, that is.)

Gave this 4 stars because of the cooking time. Like all fish you have to be careful with overcooking, tuna included. It becomes dry and unpleasent. Tuna should be nice and pink on the inside, not like the canned stuff. I sear it shut on both sides, nice and brown and then take it off of the grill and wrap it in foil and allow it to rest, the result is a nice melt in your mouth piece of fish.

text:
The marinade is excellent(!), however, there are two misguided directions in this recipe.  First, there is acid (orange juice) in this marinade and you should never marinate fish longer than 30 minutes in any marinade containing acid.  The acid denatures ("cooks") the fish like one does with ceviche.  Second, I would never grill a 4 ounce tuna steak on high for 10 to 11 minutes as the recipe suggests unless you really like your tuna dried out.

I usually don't eat tuna (and I don't know why!) and my boyfriend came home with a tuna steak, so naturally I went to my favorite recipe website, allrecipes.com, and found this one.  This marinade is very similar to the one I use for salmon so I thought I would give it a try. I am so happy I tried this recipe because tuna will now be in the weekly dinner rotation.

text:
It seems like other reviewers have been unneccesarily hard on this recipe.  The biggest problem with the recipe is the marination time.  YOU HAVE TO MARINATE FOR MORE THAN 30 MINUTES!  I recommend overnight, but atleast 3 or 4 hours is a must.  When you marinate that long it makes the tuna so juicy and tender!  It was the moistest tuna steak I had ever had, even at a restaurant.  Also be sure not to overcook the tuna, as it will dry it out.  I served it with fetucine covered in spinach cream sauce, and it made a great meal.

text:
I see a lot more tuna in my future!! 
I never marinated tuna prior to seeing this recipe. The marinade was quick and easy to put together.  The only change that I made to the recipe is that I added 2 tsp of grated fresh ginger and eliminated the oregano.  I marinated the 1" thick tuna in a zip-lock bag for 30 minutes and cooked them in a pre-heated cast iron skillet  for 5 minutes per side. (I skipped the basting)
The flavor of the marinade was very mild and did not overwhelm the tuna at all.  The tuna was just cooked through and very tender and delicious.  
I prepared it slightly reheated the next day and the flavor was even better.
This IS the best tuna steak that I've ever made!

text:
Wow..I came across this recipe, never made Tuna steaks before but was asked to.. I myself not a huge Tuna fan. 
I read over the reviews & used low sodium soy sauce with fear it would be too salty as many stated &  Garlic cloves actually used 5. Well  I doubled everything but the oregano in marinade due  to a few more Steaks to cook. BUT I let the marinade itself sit over night in fridge   I tasted in morning I thought to myself way to spicy.  I have to admit i was bit afraid to continue.  When it came to adding Tuna Steaks Marinaded for total 2 hours.  I did grill but I used Cedar wood planks where you soak -immerse planks in cold water for 2 hours , then when soaked place steaks on planks ,poured alittle marinade over them, heat grill high then turned down to approx 375 degrees & cooked 15 to 20 minutes (key is not to keep opening grill lid)  You don't turn the steaks & I was SHOCKED how good this was, I finished off by heating remaining marinade on stove (to boil) then poured over Tuna, the taste of  marinade changed completely it was so so good -I will definitely make again & again.  I'm rating 5 even though I made slight changes cause w/o this recipe I would have never attempted to try Tuna & I'll continue so as long as I use this recipe.  1 note for those who try this method take off grill 15 minutes if you like a pinkish middle/ test with fork you'll be able to tell if still too raw for your liking.  It was DEFINITELY NOT dried out.   Loved it, Thank you!!   I definitel

This was the first time I made tuna steaks. I usually order them in restaurants, but it's only because I did not know it was so easy to make at home! I did not read the other reviews before making the steaks, but had only low sodium soy sauce on hand, so that's what I used, did not have fresh herbs, so used dry, and pan seared the tuna. Out of curiosity one night we decided to try tuna steaks but didn't have a recipe. So I popped on here and found this recipe and let me tell you, we NEVER make our tuna any other way!!  The flavor is amazing & the tuna comes out so moist and delicious! We either have the tuna with a side salad or a grilled ear of corn.. so so good!! Great recipe, highly recommended!!

This recipe is a keeper.  I read the other reviews and was worried that the tuna wouldn't have any taste, so . . .I actually made/used marinade for 4 tuna steaks but only used/only had 2 tuna steaks.    Also, I made the marinade early and the tuna sat in the marinade for about 2 hours, maybe it helped the flavor, b/c they were good and, I'm not particularly easy to please.   Other than that, I had to go with dried oregano but used fresh parsely, fresh lemon juice . . .  Way too cold to grill this time of year -- I seared the tuna [sprinkling just a tiny bit of kosher salt on one side] and then put them in the broiler for a couple minutes on each side as well -- I need my fish a "little" more cooked.  They were very tender and juicy.  I would definitely make this recipe again.  Very simple and very good.  Thank you for sharing.

Outstanding!  had about 45 min. or so to marinate three large tuna steaks.  I gently pierced them with a heavy duty meat tenderizer and put the marinade and steaks in a baking pan.  I didn't have the fresh herbs so I used them in dried form, but the rest i had and also used double the garlic ;-)  Husband grilled his and my son's to rare and mine to med. to med. rare and we all agreed that these were the best tuna steaks any of us had eaten to date.  The combination of flavors went with each other so perfectly, it was as if you couldn't get enough of it, i wished I could eat it plain!  I'm thinking I'm going to try this out on steak!  You really can't go wrong with this one, the taste is just fabulous.  I will be making this marinade again for sure and probably soon on any kind of meat I make next!

Easy and excellent. Had to pan sear because I had no grill, came out great on medium high for 3-4minutes on each side then down to low, flipping/brushing every minute and 1/2.  Overcooked means dry so be vigilant! Since the tuna starts out red, a common mistake is to cook out the red. It just needs to stop being translucent to be done.

text:
I used as a base recipe. I changed it and we all LOVED it. I didn't use oregano, just didn't seem right.  Living in Hawaii, I had an orange from my tree and local caught, sashimi grade yellowfin tuna. I used lilikoi (passionfruit) juice (from my vines) instead of lemon, but think lime would be great. I added freshly grated gingerroot and a splash toasted sesame oil, only 1 tsp dried parsley.  Happened to have good low sodium tamari (hubby bought) on hand, so used that instead of cheap soy sauce.  Marinaded 3 hours, and was SO good, we mostly ate it raw as sashimi/sushi!  But, a couple guests didn't like raw fish, so I sauteed up the cut up tuna WITH the extra marinade. We all LOVED that as well.

I heated my flat cast iron comal and when it was hot I drizzled some sesame seed oil and added the tuna steaks , about 2.5 -3  minutes each side. removed from the grill and covered, letting it rest whilst I did another batch of steaks.. I also, boiled down the sauce and put a small amount of butter to it.  once thickened , I drizzled over the tuna steaks,.. I also added the sauce to our salad as well... was a perfect meal ... grazie for the recipe...

What can I say but WOW !!! I live right off the Atlantic Ocean in Humacao Puerto Rico and I've eaten fish all my life. You name it and I've had it and tuna stakes many times. But I have to say that this is THE BEST I have ever had, no questions asked. I did add a few of my own "tricks". Instead of soy sauce I used teriyaki... two tablespoons of sugar with a dash of white vinegar...I used  roasted garlic instead which adds a rich aroma... mandarin (tangerine) orange juice... also add some large shrimp with slices of fresh tangerine 2 minutes before removing the tuna. Grilled the steaks in a very hot cast iron pan with some virgin olive oil for 2 minutes 45 seconds. I like mine nice and pink on the inside.  Was it good ??? Well, I made this dish twice the very first day. That's how delicious it was. I'll be making this dish for my girlfriend which I know she will love and maybe she'll love me more. I accompanied it with steamed white rice, fried green plantains (tostones) and sweet buttered corn. After writing all this I'm hungry again....... Just try it. You won't regret it.... enjoy... bon app√©tit... buen provecho.

I can't believe I have waited this long to cook a tuna steak. I followed this recipe to the letter, with the following additions: I added a little sesame oil (half a teaspoon) and a little pureed ginger that was in the fridge. I seared over hot charcoal for almost exactly 6 minutes (3 per side). If you are a single guy looking to make something for a date night- prepare for the panties to come off. Great recipe. (Tuna was purchased from Costco)

This was the first time I've ever cooked or eaten a tuna steak and it came out DELICIOUS!  I put a 1/2 tsp of honey in the marinade, as well as a sprinkle of rosemary, as both were recommendations from previous viewers. I also used low sodium soy sauce and all dried spices (except garlic) as that is what was in the house.  My fiance and I loved it, and will be making this again and trying the marinade on other meat as well. 
I grilled my tuna steak, flipping every minute, and cooked it for 9 minutes total.  It was moist and tasty, though I will cook it for 30 sec-1 min less next time.  My fiance seared his for 3 min on each side and was very pleased.  THANKS!

I used two 4 ounce tuna steaks and marinated them in 1/3 cup orange juice (some pulp), 1/4 cup soy sauce, 3 cloves of garlic, 1 tb of honey and the spices as listed. I marinated them for an hour (flipping them over half way through) and pan seared them in the sauce and some olive oil. This made them sweet with just a taste of saltiness. Great recipe!
